     1	use bytes::Bytes;
     2	use serde::Serialize;
     3	use std::ops::Bound::{Excluded, Included, Unbounded};
     4	use std::ops::{Bound, RangeBounds};
     5	
     6	use crate::comparable_range::{ComparableRange, EndBound, StartBound};
     7	
     8	/// Concrete struct representing a range of Bytes. Gets around much of
     9	/// the cumbersome work associated with the generic trait RangeBounds<Bytes>
    10	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Eq, PartialEq, Ord, PartialOrd, Hash)]
    11	pub(crate) struct BytesRange {
    12	    inner: ComparableRange<Bytes>,
    13	}
    14	
    15	impl Serialize for BytesRange {
    16	    fn serialize<S>(&self, serializer: S) -> Result<S::Ok, S::Error>
    17	    where
    18	        S: serde::Serializer,
    19	    {
    20	        self.inner.serialize(serializer)
    21	    }
    22	}
    23	
    24	#[cfg(test)]
    25	// Checks for the annoying case when we have ("prefix", "prefix\0").
    26	// When both bounds are excluded, the range is empty even though
    27	// "prefix" < "prefix\0".
    28	pub(crate) fn is_prefix_increment(prefix: &[u8], b: &[u8]) -> bool {
    29	    if !b.starts_with(prefix.as_ref()) {
    30	        return false;
    31	    }
    32	
    33	    b[prefix.len()..] == [u8::MIN]
    34	}
    35	
    36	impl RangeBounds<Bytes> for BytesRange {
    37	    fn start_bound(&self) -> Bound<&Bytes> {
    38	        self.inner.start_bound()
    39	    }
    40	
    41	    fn end_bound(&self) -> Bound<&Bytes> {
    42	        self.inner.end_bound()
    43	    }
    44	}
    45	
    46	fn is_bound_non_empty(bound: &Bound<Bytes>) -> bool {
    47	    match bound {
    48	        Included(b) | Excluded(b) => !b.is_empty(),
    49	        Unbounded => true,
    50	    }
    51	}
    52	
    53	impl BytesRange {
    54	    pub(crate) fn new(start_bound: Bound<Bytes>, end_bound: Bound<Bytes>) -> Self {
    55	        assert!(
    56	            is_bound_non_empty(&start_bound),
    57	            "Start bound must be non-empty"
    58	        );
    59	        assert!(
    60	            is_bound_non_empty(&end_bound),
    61	            "End bound must be non-empty"
    62	        );
    63	        let inner = ComparableRange::new(start_bound, end_bound);
    64	        assert!(inner.non_empty(), "Range must be non-empty");
    65	        Self { inner }
    66	    }
    67	
    68	    pub(crate) fn new_empty() -> Self {
    69	        Self {
    70	            inner: ComparableRange::new(
    71	                Excluded(Bytes::copy_from_slice(&[0_u8])),
    72	                Excluded(Bytes::copy_from_slice(&[0_u8])),
    73	            ),
    74	        }
    75	    }
    76	
    77	    pub(crate) fn from<T: RangeBounds<Bytes>>(range: T) -> Self {
    78	        Self::new(range.start_bound().cloned(), range.end_bound().cloned())
    79	    }
    80	
    81	    pub(crate) fn from_slice<'a, T>(range: T) -> Self
    82	    where
    83	        T: RangeBounds<&'a [u8]>,
    84	    {
    85	        Self::new(
    86	            range.start_bound().map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b)),
    87	            range.end_bound().map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b)),
    88	        )
    89	    }
    90	
    91	    /// Build a half-open range `[prefix, prefix+1)` covering all keys that start with
    92	    /// `prefix`.
    93	    ///
    94	    /// - Empty prefix returns `(..)` so callers can scan the entire keyspace.
    95	    /// - If the prefix is all `0xff`, the end bound is unbounded rather than overflowing.
    96	    pub(crate) fn from_prefix(prefix: &[u8]) -> Self {
    97	        if prefix.is_empty() {
    98	            return Self::new(Unbounded, Unbounded);
    99	        }
   100	
   101	        let start = Bytes::copy_from_slice(prefix);
   102	        let end = Self::increment_prefix(prefix)
   103	            .map(Excluded)
   104	            .unwrap_or(Unbounded);
   105	        Self::new(Included(start), end)
   106	    }
   107	
   108	    /// Compute the smallest byte string that is lexicographically greater than any key
   109	    /// starting with `prefix`. Returns `None` when `prefix` is all `0xff`.
   110	    fn increment_prefix(prefix: &[u8]) -> Option<Bytes> {
   111	        let mut upper_bound = prefix.to_vec();
   112	
   113	        for i in (0..upper_bound.len()).rev() {
   114	            if upper_bound[i] != u8::MAX {
   115	                upper_bound[i] += 1;
   116	                upper_bound.truncate(i + 1);
   117	                return Some(Bytes::from(upper_bound));
   118	            }
   119	        }
   120	
   121	        None
   122	    }
   123	
   124	    #[cfg(test)]
   125	    pub(crate) fn from_ref<K, T>(range: T) -> Self
   126	    where
   127	        K: AsRef<[u8]>,
   128	        T: RangeBounds<K>,
   129	    {
   130	        let start = range
   131	            .start_bound()
   132	            .map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b.as_ref()));
   133	        let end = range
   134	            .end_bound()
   135	            .map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b.as_ref()));
   136	        Self::new(start, end)
   137	    }
   138	
   139	    pub(crate) fn intersect(&self, other: &Self) -> Option<Self> {
   140	        self.inner
   141	            .intersect(&other.inner)
   142	            .map(|inner| Self { inner })
   143	    }
   144	
   145	    pub(crate) fn is_start_bound_included_or_unbounded(&self) -> bool {
   146	        !matches!(self.start_bound(), Excluded(_))
   147	    }
   148	
   149	    #[cfg(test)]
   150	    pub(crate) fn non_empty(&self) -> bool {
   151	        self.inner.non_empty()
   152	    }
   153	
   154	    #[cfg(test)]
   155	    pub(crate) fn empty(&self) -> bool {
   156	        !self.inner.non_empty()
   157	    }
   158	
   159	    pub(crate) fn comparable_start_bound(&self) -> StartBound<&Bytes> {
   160	        self.inner.comparable_start_bound()
   161	    }
   162	
   163	    pub(crate) fn comparable_end_bound(&self) -> EndBound<&Bytes> {
   164	        self.inner.comparable_end_bound()
   165	    }
   166	
   167	    pub(crate) fn as_point(&self) -> Option<&Bytes> {
   168	        match (self.start_bound(), self.end_bound()) {
   169	            (Bound::Included(start), Bound::Included(end)) if start == end => Some(start),
   170	            _ => None,
   171	        }
   172	    }
   173	}

   141	fn cmp_bound<T: Ord>(a: &Bound<T>, b: &Bound<T>, start: bool) -> Ordering {
   142	    match (a, b) {
   143	        (Bound::Included(a), Bound::Included(b)) | (Bound::Excluded(a), Bound::Excluded(b)) => {
   144	            a.cmp(b)
   145	        }
   146	        (Bound::Included(a), Bound::Excluded(b)) => match a.cmp(b) {
   147	            Ordering::Equal => {
   148	                if start {
   149	                    Ordering::Less
   150	                } else {
   151	                    Ordering::Greater
   152	                }
   153	            }
   154	            other => other,
   155	        },
   156	        (Bound::Excluded(a), Bound::Included(b)) => match a.cmp(b) {
   157	            Ordering::Equal => {
   158	                if start {
   159	                    Ordering::Greater
   160	                } else {
   161	                    Ordering::Less
   162	                }
   163	            }
   164	            other => other,
   165	        },
   166	        (Bound::Unbounded, Bound::Unbounded) => Ordering::Equal,
   167	        (Bound::Unbounded, _) => {
   168	            if start {
   169	                Ordering::Less
   170	            } else {
   171	                Ordering::Greater
   172	            }
   173	        }
   174	        (_, Bound::Unbounded) => {
   175	            if start {
   176	                Ordering::Greater
   177	            } else {
   178	                Ordering::Less
   179	            }
   180	        }
   181	    }
   182	}

   223	
   224	    pub(crate) fn intersect(&self, other: &Self) -> Option<Self> {
   225	        let max_start = max(&self.start, &other.start);
   226	        let min_end = min(&self.end, &other.end);
   227	        let intersection = Self {
   228	            start: max_start.clone(),
   229	            end: min_end.clone(),
   230	        };
   231	        if intersection.non_empty() {
   232	            Some(intersection)
   233	        } else {
   234	            None
   235	        }
   236	    }
   237	
   238	    #[allow(dead_code)]
   239	    pub(crate) fn union(&self, other: &Self) -> Option<Self> {
   240	        // Sort the ranges to make the function commutative
   241	        let (first, second) = if self < other {
   242	            (self, other)
   243	        } else {
   244	            (other, self)
   245	        };
   246	        // If the ranges are not intersecting and they are not adjacent, no union is possible
   247	        if first.intersect(second).is_none() && !first.are_adjacent(second) {
   248	            return None;
   249	        }
   250	        // Take the minimum of start bounds and maximum of end bounds
   251	        Some(Self {
   252	            start: min(&first.start, &other.start).clone(),
   253	            end: max(&first.end, &second.end).clone(),
   254	        })
   255	    }

   258	        match (&self.end.inner, &other.start.inner) {
   259	            (Bound::Included(a), Bound::Excluded(b)) => a == b,
   260	            (Bound::Excluded(a), Bound::Included(b)) => a == b,

   306	pub(crate) mod tests {
   307	
   308	    use std::{
   309	        cmp::Ordering,
   310	        ops::{Bound, RangeBounds},
   311	    };
   312	
   313	    use rand::seq::SliceRandom;
   314	    use rstest::rstest;
   315	
   316	    use crate::comparable_range::{ComparableRange, EndBound, StartBound};
   317	
   318	    struct TestCase(Bound<u32>, Bound<u32>, Ordering);
   319	
   320	    #[rstest]
   321	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Included(1), Bound::Included(1), Ordering::Equal))]
   322	    // [1, 100) vs. (1, 100) => (1 <= n < 100) vs. (1 < n < 100)
   323	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Included(1), Bound::Excluded(1), Ordering::Less))]
   324	    // (1, 100) vs. [1, 100) =>  (1 < n < 100) vs. (1 <= n < 100)
   325	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Excluded(1), Bound::Included(1), Ordering::Greater))]
   326	    // For start bound, unbounded represents -Inf
   327	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Unbounded, Bound::Included(1), Ordering::Less))]
   328	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Unbounded, Bound::Excluded(1), Ordering::Less))]
   329	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Included(1), Bound::Unbounded, Ordering::Greater))]
   330	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Excluded(1), Bound::Unbounded, Ordering::Greater))]
   331	    fn test_start_bound_cmp(#[case] test_case: TestCase) {
   332	        let lhs = StartBound::from(test_case.0);
   333	        let rhs = StartBound::from(test_case.1);
   334	        assert_eq!(lhs.cmp(&rhs), test_case.2);
   335	    }
   336	
   337	    #[rstest]
   338	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Included(100), Bound::Included(100), Ordering::Equal))]
   339	    // (1, 100] vs. (1, 100) => (1 < n <= 100) vs. (1 < n < 100)
   340	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Included(100), Bound::Excluded(100), Ordering::Greater))]
   341	    // (1, 100) vs. (1, 100] =>  (1 < n < 100) vs. (1 < n <= 100)
   342	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Excluded(100), Bound::Included(100), Ordering::Less))]
   343	    // For end bound, unbounded represents +Inf
   344	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Unbounded, Bound::Included(1), Ordering::Greater))]
   345	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Unbounded, Bound::Excluded(1), Ordering::Greater))]
   346	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Included(1), Bound::Unbounded, Ordering::Less))]
   347	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Excluded(1), Bound::Unbounded, Ordering::Less))]
   348	    fn test_end_bound_cmp(#[case] test_case: TestCase) {
   349	        let lhs = EndBound::from(test_case.0);
   350	        let rhs = EndBound::from(test_case.1);
   351	        assert_eq!(lhs.cmp(&rhs), test_case.2);
   352	    }
   353	
   354	    #[test]
   355	    fn test_range() {
   356	        let ranges = vec![
   357	            ComparableRange::from_range(..10),
   358	            ComparableRange::from_range(..1000),
   359	            ComparableRange::from_range(..),
   360	            ComparableRange::from_range(1..5),
   361	            ComparableRange::from_range(1..10),
   362	            ComparableRange::from_range(1..),
   363	            ComparableRange::from_range(2..3),
   364	            ComparableRange::from_range(2..),
   365	            ComparableRange::from_range(100..123),
   366	        ];
   367	        let mut shuffled_ranges = ranges.clone();
   368	        // Shuffle the ranges to ensure the order is random
   369	        shuffled_ranges.shuffle(&mut rand::rng());
   370	        // Sort the ranges to ensure the order is deterministic
   371	        shuffled_ranges.sort();
   372	
   373	        assert_eq!(shuffled_ranges, ranges);
   374	    }
   375	
   376	    struct TwoRangeOperation<T: Ord + Clone> {
   377	        first: ComparableRange<T>,
   378	        second: ComparableRange<T>,
   379	        result: Option<ComparableRange<T>>,
   380	    }

   197	    pub async fn scan_with_options<K, T>(
   198	        &self,
   199	        range: T,
   200	        options: &ScanOptions,
   201	    ) -> Result<DbIterator, crate::Error>
   202	    where
   203	        K: AsRef<[u8]> + Send,
   204	        T: RangeBounds<K> + Send,
   205	    {
   206	        // TODO: this range conversion logic can be extract to an util
   207	        let start = range
   208	            .start_bound()
   209	            .map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b.as_ref()));
   210	        let end = range
   211	            .end_bound()
   212	            .map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b.as_ref()));
   213	        let range = (start, end);
   214	
   215	        // Track read range for SSI conflict detection if needed
   216	        let range_tracker = if self.isolation_level == IsolationLevel::SerializableSnapshot {
   217	            let tracker = Arc::new(DbIteratorRangeTracker::new());
   218	            self.range_trackers.lock().push(tracker.clone());
   219	            Some(tracker)
   220	        } else {
   221	            None
   222	        };
   223	
   224	        self.db_inner.check_closed()?;
   225	        let db_state = self.db_inner.state.read().view();
   226	
   227	        // Clone the WriteBatch for the scan to ensure that the scan within a transaction
   228	        // sees a consistent view of the current writes.
   229	        let write_batch_cloned = self.write_batch.read().clone();
   230	
   231	        // For now, delegate to the underlying reader
   232	        self.db_inner
   233	            .reader
   234	            .scan_with_options(
   235	                BytesRange::from(range),
   236	                options,
   237	                &db_state,
   238	                Some(write_batch_cloned),
   239	                Some(self.started_seq),
   240	                range_tracker,

use slatedb::object_store::{memory::InMemory, ObjectStore};
use slatedb::Db;
use std::sync::Arc;

#[tokio::main]
async fn main() -> Result<(), slatedb::Error> {
    let object_store: Arc<dyn ObjectStore> = Arc::new(InMemory::new());
    let db = Db::open("/repro_empty_bounds", object_store).await?;
    db.put(b"a", b"1").await?;

    // This is the important bit: callers can supply RangeBounds whose
    // start/end bounds are empty byte slices. BytesRange currently panics.
    let mut iter = db.scan(b"".as_slice()..=b"".as_slice()).await?;
    assert!(iter.next().await?.is_none());
    db.close().await?;
    Ok(())
}
RS
cargo run --manifest-path /tmp/slatedb-repro-empty-bounds/Cargo.toml -q
EOF

   680	    /// use slatedb::{Db, Error};
   681	    /// use slatedb::object_store::{ObjectStore, memory::InMemory};
   682	    /// use std::sync::Arc;
   683	    ///
   684	    /// #[tokio::main]
   685	    /// async fn main() -> Result<(), Error> {
   686	    ///     let object_store: Arc<dyn ObjectStore> = Arc::new(InMemory::new());
   687	    ///     let db = Db::open("test_db", object_store).await?;
   688	    ///     db.close().await?;
   689	    ///     Ok(())
   690	    /// }
   691	    /// ```
   692	    pub async fn close(&self) -> Result<(), crate::Error> {
   693	        let should_flush = match self.status().close_reason {
   694	            // If already closed, don't close again.
   695	            Some(CloseReason::Clean) => return Err(SlateDBError::Closed.into()),
   696	            // If in failed state, allow close, but don't flush since the database
   697	            // might be in a bad state. Note that multiple close() calls will always
   698	            // run when in a failed state (vs. a clean closure, which will return
   699	            // Error::Closed(CloseReason::Clean) on subsequent calls).
   700	            Some(_) => false,
   701	            // Flush outstanding writes if the database is still open.
   702	            None => true,
   703	        };
   704	
   705	        // Mark the database as closed before flushing.
   706	        self.inner.status_manager.write_result(Ok(()));
   707	
   708	        if should_flush {
   709	            if let Err(e) = self.inner.flush(false).await {
   710	                warn!("failed to flush db during close [error={:?}]", e);
   711	            }
   712	        }
   713	
   714	        MemtableFlusher::shutdown(&self.task_executor).await;
   715	
   716	        if let Err(e) = self.task_executor.shutdown_task(COMPACTOR_TASK_NAME).await {
   717	            warn!("failed to shutdown compactor task [error={:?}]", e);
   718	        }
   719	
   720	        if let Err(e) = self.task_executor.shutdown_task(GC_TASK_NAME).await {
   721	            warn!("failed to shutdown garbage collector task [error={:?}]", e);
   722	        }
   723	
   724	        if let Err(e) = self
   725	            .task_executor
   726	            .shutdown_task(WRITE_BATCH_TASK_NAME)
   727	            .await
   728	        {
   729	            warn!("failed to shutdown writer task [error={:?}]", e);
   730	        }
   731	
   732	        if let Err(e) = self.task_executor.shutdown_task(WAL_BUFFER_TASK_NAME).await {
   733	            warn!("failed to shutdown wal writer task [error={:?}]", e);
   734	        }
   735	
   736	        info!("db closed");
   737	        Ok(())
   738	    }
   739

   766	    ///

   769	    ///
   770	    ///     // Snapshot still sees old state, original db sees new data
   771	    ///     assert_eq!(snapshot.get(b"key2").await?, None);
   772	    ///     assert_eq!(db.get(b"key2").await?, Some(Bytes::from(b"value2".as_ref())));
   773	    ///
   774	    ///     Ok(())
   775	    /// }
   776	    /// ```
   777	    pub async fn snapshot(&self) -> Result<Arc<DbSnapshot>, crate::Error> {
   778	        self.inner.check_closed()?;
   779	        let snapshot = DbSnapshot::new(self.inner.clone(), None);
   780	        Ok(snapshot)
   781	    }

   783	    /// Get a value from the database with default read options.
   784	    ///
   785	    /// The `Bytes` object returned contains a slice of an entire
   786	    /// 4 KiB block. The block will be held in memory as long as the
   787	    /// caller holds a reference to the `Bytes` object. Consider
   788	    /// copying the data if you need to hold it for a long time.
   789	    ///
   790	    /// ## Arguments
   791	    /// - `key`: the key to get
   792	    ///
   793	    /// ## Returns
   794	    /// - `Result<Option<Bytes>, Error>`:
   795	    ///     - `Some(Bytes)`: the value if it exists
   796	    ///     - `None`: if the value does not exist
   797	    ///
   798	    /// ## Errors
   799	    /// - `Error`: if there was an error getting the value
   800	    ///
   801	    /// ## Examples
   802	    ///
   803	    /// ```
   804	    /// use slatedb::{Db, Error};
   805	    /// use slatedb::object_store::{ObjectStore, memory::InMemory};
   806	    /// use std::sync::Arc;
   807	    ///
   808	    /// #[tokio::main]
   809	    /// async fn main() -> Result<(), Error> {
   810	    ///     let object_store: Arc<dyn ObjectStore> = Arc::new(InMemory::new());
   811	    ///     let db = Db::open("test_db", object_store).await?;
   812	    ///     db.put(b"key", b"value").await?;
   813	    ///     assert_eq!(db.get(b"key").await?, Some("value".into()));
   814	    ///     Ok(())
   815	    /// }
   816	    /// ```
   817	    pub async fn get<K: AsRef<[u8]> + Send>(&self, key: K) -> Result<Option<Bytes>, crate::Error> {
   818	        self.get_with_options(key, &ReadOptions::default()).await
   819	    }

   821	    /// Get a value from the database with custom read options.
   822	    ///
   823	    /// The `Bytes` object returned contains a slice of an entire
   824	    /// 4 KiB block. The block will be held in memory as long as the
   825	    /// caller holds a reference to the `Bytes` object. Consider
   826	    /// copying the data if you need to hold it for a long time.
   827	    ///
   828	    /// ## Arguments
   829	    /// - `key`: the key to get
   830	    /// - `options`: the read options to use (Note that [`ReadOptions::read_level`] has no effect for readers, which
   831	    ///   can only observe committed state).
   832	    ///

    78	    }
    79	
    80	    fn nonempty_partial_bounded_range(size: usize) -> impl Strategy<Value = BytesRange> {
    81	        nonempty_bytes(size).prop_flat_map(|a| {
    82	            prop_oneof![
    83	                Just(BytesRange::new(Unbounded, Included(a.clone()))),
    84	                Just(BytesRange::new(Unbounded, Excluded(a.clone()))),
    85	                Just(BytesRange::new(Included(a.clone()), Unbounded)),
    86	                Just(BytesRange::new(Excluded(a), Unbounded)),
    87	            ]
    88	        })
    89	    }
    90	
    91	    fn extend_bytes(a: &Bytes, value: u8) -> Bytes {
    92	        let mut b = BytesMut::from(a.as_ref());
    93	        b.put_u8(value);
    94	        b.freeze()
    95	    }
    96	
    97	    fn arbitrary_single_point_bounded_range(size: usize) -> impl Strategy<Value = BytesRange> {
    98	        nonempty_bytes(size).prop_flat_map(|a| {
    99	            let a_extended = extend_bytes(&a, u8::MIN);
   100	            prop_oneof![
   101	                Just(BytesRange::new(Included(a.clone()), Included(a.clone()))),
   102	                Just(BytesRange::new(
   103	                    Included(a.clone()),
   104	                    Excluded(a_extended.clone())
   105	                )),
   106	                Just(BytesRange::new(Excluded(a), Included(a_extended))),
   107	            ]
   108	        })
   109	    }
   110	
   111	    fn min_and_max(a: Bytes, b: Bytes) -> (Bytes, Bytes) {
   112	        if a < b {
   113	            (a, b)
   114	        } else {
   115	            (b, a)
   116	        }
   117	    }
   118	
   119	    fn nonempty_range_filter(tuple: (Bytes, Bytes)) -> Option<(Bytes, Bytes)> {
   120	        let (a, b) = tuple;
   121	        if a == b {
   122	            None
   123	        } else {
   124	            let (start, end) = min_and_max(a, b);
   125	            if bytes_range::is_prefix_increment(&start, &end) {
   126	                None
   127	            } else {
   128	                Some((start, end))
   129	            }
   130	        }
   131	    }
   132	
   133	    pub(crate) fn empty_range(size: usize) -> impl Strategy<Value = BytesRange> {
   134	        nonempty_bytes(size).prop_flat_map(|a| {
   135	            prop_oneof![
   136	                Just(BytesRange::new(Excluded(a.clone()), Excluded(a.clone()))),
   137	                Just(BytesRange::new(Included(a.clone()), Excluded(a.clone()))),
   138	                Just(BytesRange::new(Excluded(a.clone()), Included(a))),
   139	            ]
   140	        })
   141	    }
   142	
   143	    pub(crate) fn nonempty_range(size: usize) -> impl Strategy<Value = BytesRange> {
   144	        prop_oneof![
   145	            Just(BytesRange::new(Unbounded, Unbounded)),
   146	            arbitrary_single_point_bounded_range(size),
   147	            nonempty_partial_bounded_range(size),
   148	            nonempty_bounded_range(size),
   149	        ]
   150	    }
